nt gn bk">One, if not the main, challenge with producing good intelligence is to have access to the right information at the right moment. The right telemetry from the right angle helps you to detect and dig out the right signal. Sometimes, in order to obtain good telemetry, you need a bit of luck .</p><p id="c2d2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The story we are writing here will try to explain how, from a simple mistake made by an operator, we managed to collect and exploit a lot of precious information from a “Fast Flux” network called <strong class="my gv">BraZZZerS Fast Flux </strong>between end of 2018 and 2022.</p><p id="43e9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">After sharing this data as TLP:amber with partners for years, the service now going into decline and the misconfiguration finally being fixed, we think it is now the right time to release this data and explain what can be found inside. It is a good occasion to try to fill any holes in your documentation and keep track of the technical facts about the cybercrime history.</p><h2 id="beaf" class="nu nv gu bf nw nx ny dy nz oa ob ea oc panel</figcaption></figure><p id="f3d2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">BraZZZers is just another domain protection service like <a class="af pr" href="https://krebsonsecurity.com/2019/07/meet-the-worlds-biggest-bulletproof-hoster/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Yalishanda</a> or even <a class="af pr" href="https://www.proofpoint.com/us/threat-insight/post/sandiflux-another-fast-flux-infrastructure-used-malware-distribution-emerges" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Sandiflux/Fluxxy</a>.</p><p id="4160" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In order to find and track BraZZZers clients in the wild, we had to make sure that the fast flux we were observing was really BraZZZers and not one of the other similar services. In December 2018, an announcement made on the forum BHF helped us to understand where to look in order to find BraZZZers nodes.</p><figure class="ow ox oy oz pa pb ot ou paragraph-image"><div nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">19 Dec 2018<br/>In connection with recent events, the fact that the author decided to completely close the sale and support of software, people are already appearing on the Internet forums who speculate on this situation. Please be vigilant.<br/>I decided to create one topic, which will be considered official and unified in order not to produce a lot of topics when questions arise.</p><p id="545a" class="mw mx os my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The author left us a builder so that we could rebuild further our clients. Don’t panic :)</p><p id="d099" class="mw mx os my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Let’s, in case of any questions about the software, ask them here, answer each other, to the point and without unnecessary flooding, please.</p><p id="2de0" class="mw mx os my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">I propose to exterminate the rats, to prevent them from getting rich on the panic in the market.</p></blockquote><p id="0057" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">At the end of 2018, the manager of the Azorult stealer gave up on the project and left a builder to the BraZZZers admins.</p><p id="5cd9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Similar signs came from the managers of the password stealer KPOT who where directly reselling BraZZZers with the KPOT package:</p><blockquote class="pd pe pf"><p id="f807" class="mw mx os my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The price now is $ 75, but you can still buy at the old price ($ 65) in the case of buying a pre-installed KPOT on the BraZZZerS hosting. The price for everything will be $ 215 and $ 150 for each subsequent month of hosting. When buying a pre-installed version, you immediately get a ready-to-work admin and build, initially configured for a bit domain, change it if necessary. The number of pre-installed versions is limited!</p></blockquote><p id="672a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Thanks to those posts and several other intel signals (like the association to MoreneHost) we managed to attribute the correct IPs and map the BraZZZers network.</p><h2 id="95c1" class="nu nv gu bf nw nx ny dy nz oa ob ea oc nh od oe of nl og oh oi np oj ok ol om bk">Mapping BraZZZers nodes</h2><p id="b147" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz on nb nc nd oo nf ng nh op nj nk nl oq nn no np or nr ns nt gn bk">Mapping the BraZZZers infrastructure is actually quite simple.</p><p id="05e4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The first and easiest way is to use passive DNS.</p><ul class=""><li id="fcdc" class="mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt pt pu pv bk">You identify a BraZZZers customer</li><li id="fc1a" class="mw mx gu my b mz pw nb nc nd px nf ng nh py nj nk nl pz nn no np qa nr ns nt pt pu pv bk">You resolve their domains</li><li id="8017" class="mw mx gu my b mz pw nb nc nd px nf ng nh py nj nk nl pz nn no np qa nr ns nt pt pu pv bk">You use pDNS on the IPs (BraZZZers nodes are shared between customers)</li><li id="f305" class="mw mx gu my b mz pw nb nc nd px nf ng nh py nj nk nl pz nn no np qa nr ns nt pt pu pv bk">You pivot until covering the maximum of IPs.</li></ul><p id="35c4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">However, the pDNS method has its limits for mapping infrastructure since you can only discover known DNS resolutions and must to be very careful with the time frame while pivoting in pDNS.</p><p id="a0ff" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">In the same way, we quickly observed that since 2018, BraZZZers used the same TLS certificate for its nodes:</p><p id="cebf" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">03:21:56:e1:5c:92:6a:e6:3d:a4:c1:b6:51:54:c3:ff:cc:35</p><p id="2be1" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">You can then use your favorite mass scan provider and look for new IPs.</p><figure class="ow ox oy oz pa pb ot ou paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="ph pi fj pj bh pk"><div class="ot nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">We also realized that every BraZZZers node uses the hostname “ns4.dnsdns.gdns”, which makes the nodes searchable for mass scan providers and then pDNS pivot is possible.</p><p id="421b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Yet, we found an even better way to map the network. By analyzing each node of the infrastructure we discovered an interesting Nginx configuration problem.</p><h2 id="d5b6" class="nu nv gu bf nw nx ny dy nz oa ob ea oc nh od oe of nl og oh oi np oj ok ol om bk"><strong class="al">The Nginx misconfiguration</strong></h2><p id="30af" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz on nb nc nd oo nf ng nh op nj nk nl oq nn no np or nr ns nt gn bk">While configuring the deployment of a new node for protecting domains, the Nginx vhost configuration was setup to disable error_log logging.</p><p id="09f5" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The admins edited the Nginx configuration file by setting “error_log off” where “off” should actually be <strong class="my gv">a path.</strong> The way the virtual hosts were configured ended up writing the error_log in a file called “off” in the html directory!</p><figure class="ow ox oy oz pa pb ot ou class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">By looking at that log we can understand that it’s a request sent from a <a class="af pr" href="https://check-host.net/" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">check-host account</a>, a web service used to monitor the up-time of a domain.</p><p id="9910" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The second kind is less interesting but still leak a lot of information, it’s basic error_log information. Every 404 detected on the nodes (you can see a lot of mass web crawlers mass scanning IPs for example). These errors are often generated when a domain is resolving to a BraZZZers node and that node doesn&#x27;t have a virtual host configured for the domain. id="6573" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">After understanding the value of that data, we quickly built different tools to store and parse those logs and just like that started a very interesting 4 years journey.</p><p id="312f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">As a reminder, these logs represent a very small fraction of the BraZZZers traffic. We only catch the requests that have failed. If we compare the number of requests collected on BraZZZers with a botnet like Dreambot and the effective traffic captured on the control server, the error_logs represent less than 5% of the total traffic; but those 5% are still gold.</p><p id="0215" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">We will now try to describe a few use cases observable in these logs in order to demonstrate what kind of data are available.</p><h2 id="d3bb" class="nu nv gu bf nw nx ny dy nz oa ob ea oc nh od oe of nl og oh oi np oj ok ol om bk">Use cases</h2><p id="c4f6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz on nb nc nd oo nf ng nh op nj nk nl oq nn no np or nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">Nemty ransomware and JWT leak</strong></p><p id="44c7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Nemty was using BraZZZers to protect its domains nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">A simple config mistake from BraZZZers ended up compromising the whole operation. Like most of the other clients of BraZZZers, Nemty trusted the service to hide their backend and didn’t take any extra precaution to hide the real IP from the BraZZZers network.</p><p id="b245" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">The hidden panel of Azorult</strong></p><p id="e819" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The leaked BraZZZers logs has been particularly handy with the Azorult stealer. In order to protect the webpanel of Azorult, the developers of the stealer forced the installation of the webpanel into a web directory with a random name (I.E. domain.com/fsebkjfxbefxdrhvbrghjkvb/admin.php)</p><p id="3fe3" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">This random name makes it theoretically impossible for anybody to guess the webpanel URL.</p><p id="b0db" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">When the Azorult project was abandoned, the malware was still very active in the wild and omnipresent around BraZZZers infrastructure.</p><figure class="ow ox oy oz pa pb ot ou ns nt gn bk">One of the most interesting clients of BraZZZers is for sure ISFB. We observed several branches of ISFB using BraZZZers to hide its domains, the most active branch was <a class="af pr" rel="noopener" href="/csis-techblog/the-end-of-dreambot-a-loved-piece-of-gozi-24cc9bfc8122">Dreambot</a>. nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Requests like this were very typical for ISFB bots. With Dreambot, the port 80 of the control server was reserved for the bots and the port 3000 for the panel.</p><p id="18c4" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Even if we imagine that the Dreambot operators were using basic security like, for example, not using admin:admin as credentials, the BraZZZers requests acted like a sinkhole and allowed us to capture and analyse lots of Dreambot campaigns and alert victims.</p><p id="41a6" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">When BraZZZers leaked a log like:</p><blockquote class="pd pe pf"><p id="9fae" class="mw mx os my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">http://anti-doping.at/images/W7DM8fQnAkZl5/w_2BSbbA/6KBhhx7wg5evMuvuMv1oao4/U6yRGzURZD/XiL01nc5vbfiBN4bX/1hU3GL4_2F8A/_2Br5AtZAwV/A9odyEI1ZXMvvh/PyF7OtEFdbtoa6ixqh_2F/kovs8YDK7vDDr2cc/iLrdTIARsyp9z_2/FT_2BFFd_2BUGwOjfW/ZEZOwXx.gif</p></blockquote><p id="c258" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">We could easily (thanks here to <a class="af pr" href="https://twitter.com/fumik0_" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Fumiko</a>) parse those requests and extract campaigns data without even having to look for a binary:</p><figure nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">Cryptbot Stealer</strong></p><p id="303b" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Another cool piece of malware to follow in these logs is <a class="af pr" href="https://www.gdatasoftware.com/blog/2020/02/35802-bitbucket-abused-as-malware-slinger" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">Cryptbot</a>. The operator of Cryptbot managed to build a huge botnet hidden behind a quite resilient infrastructure. It has been very hard to obtain intel - until we looked at BraZZZers.</p><p id="bb77" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">We can observe the early days of Cryptbot dating back to 2019. Thanks to the upstream we were able to monitor them using the same IP as central CnC for months: 5.182.39[.]172.</p><p id="2c88" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">If you do a reverse lookup and look for all the domains configured to that IP, you will see that Cryptbot in its early days was hosting its own marketplace in order to resell their stolen logs.</p><figure class="ow ox oy oz pa pb ot ou paragraph-image"><div role="button" tabindex="0" class="ph pi fj pj bh pk"><div class="ot ou qt"><picture><source mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Month after month you can observe the botnet evolving into multiple botnets split on different infrastructures.</p><p id="64f2" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">This is just another example of how useful these logs can be. Looking up every domain attached to the same hidden IP is a great way to help your attribution. Lots of actors were sloppy with real server IPs, thinking they were protected by BraZZZers.</p><p id="446d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><strong class="my gv">Marketplaces</strong></p><p id="f8ae" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">BraZZZers was not only reserved to malware, we observed a fair amount of Market places / carding shops. extract valuable data. https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:828/1*Gao4lWXW6Ok9ajquz44e3Q.png 828w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:1100/1*Gao4lWXW6Ok9ajquz44e3Q.png 1100w, https://miro.medium.com/v2/resize:fit:742/1*Gao4lWXW6Ok9ajquz44e3Q.png 742w" sizes="(min-resolution: 4dppx) and (max-width: 700px) 50vw, (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 4) and (max-width: 700px) 50vw, (min-resolution: 3dppx) and (max-width: 700px) 67vw, (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 3) and (max-width: 700px) 65vw, (min-resolution: 2.5dppx) and (max-width: 700px) 80vw, (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2.5) and (max-width: 700px) 80vw, (min-resolution: 2dppx) and (max-width: 700px) 100vw, (-webkit-min-device-pixel-ratio: 2) and (max-width: 700px) 100vw, 371px"/><img alt="" class="bh md pc c" width="371" height="540" loading="lazy" role="presentation"/></picture></div><figcaption class="pl ff pm ot ou pn po bf b bg z du">Top hosters used to host the BraZZZers proxy nodes</figcaption></figure><p id="a10c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">This story teach us that nobody is immune from a incompetent supply chain. It’s a good example of the limits of the open cybercrime industry. The business is mainly based on trust and reviews and we have seen several cases where BraZZZers admins were pushing fake reviews to boost the reputation of the service. From here it’s the snow ball effect and it just needs one big name like Azorult or a ransomware group patient enough to tolerate the poor quality service to attract more clients.</p><p id="2a38" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">While following the business side of BraZZZers, we observed several users reporting the poor quality of the service, the grey links to the hosting company MoreneHost or the low frequency of nodes renewal but that hasn’t been enough to scare away the majority of customers.</p><p id="b993" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">We expect to see more and more cases like this one. The cybercrime industry is growing much faster than the skills of the cyber criminals. Almost every step of fraudulent activity is now supported by a third party within the market. Malware, VNC, infrastructure, drop data, drops, marketplaces. The industry end up with a multitude of poorly developed services sold in open marketplaces to customers completely unable to understand if a service should be trusted or not as long as it works.</p><h2 id="4a12" class="nu nv gu bf nw nx ny dy nz oa ob ea oc nh od oe of nl og oh oi np oj ok ol om bk">Opening the data</h2><p id="b51a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz on nb nc nd oo nf ng nh op nj nk nl oq nn no np or nr ns nt gn bk">As explained in the introduction, the data is composed of upstream and 404 logs from end of 2018 to March 2022. To make the interesting data available, while trying not to expose victims IPs, we are opening all the upstream logs without client IPs as TLP;WHITE.</p><p id="f84d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">The file is a csv: date,domain,upstream,referrer.</p><p id="e08c" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk"><a class="af pr" href="https://benkow.cc/braZZZersUpstream2018-2022_.zip" rel="noopener ugc nofollow" target="_blank">[Download]</a> — Zip password: infected</p><p id="2b73" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">ef2a69c94e5420f44ee0932abbfaf8e3b4f5f5bb6308a4928dc4dd4bc06f6d4c</p><p id="f5b3" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">We hope these logs will maybe make somebody out there able to look at them from yet another angle.</p><p id="1a78" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mw mx gu my b mz na nb nc nd ne nf ng nh ni nj nk nl nm nn no np nq nr ns nt gn bk">Happy hunting!</p></div></div></div></div></section></div></div></article></div><div class="ab cb"><div class="ci bh fz ga gb gc"><div class="qz ra ab ja"><div
